Mander then asked the British government to monitor the Chinese government’s fulfillment of its obligations to Britain. Eden agreed.

News Briefs

The Antecedents and Consequences of the Red Peril in Fujian (A Xiamen Dispatch) 75

Before addressing the main topic, I must make a few preliminary remarks. My hometown is in southern Fujian, and I have been living on Gulangyu Island, residing in Southeast Asia, for nearly twenty years. Now, seeing the Red bandits first occupy Tinglong, then capture Zhangzhou, with Xiamen and Quanzhou also in imminent danger, I fear that if rescue is not swift, the entire province of Fujian will soon become a red world. Fujian, especially southern Fujian, is the ancestral home of millions of overseas Chinese in the islands of Southeast Asia, the Philippines, and territories of Britain, the Netherlands, America, France, and Siam. Who does not have a hometown? Who does not have relatives? Who does not have ancestral graves? How can we bear to sit idly by and watch it sink, witnessing the present, reflecting on the past, and fearing the future? I earnestly hope that my millions of Fujianese overseas Chinese will investigate the root causes of the problem and rise together to save it. Then we shall be fortunate indeed.

The areas of western and southern Fujian now occupied by the Red Army have established so-called Soviet governments and are implementing their destructive measures, including burning, killing, looting, raping, confiscating private property, and destroying contracts. These tragic scenes have already unfolded one after another. The people of Ting, Zhang, and Long are suffering the pain of family destruction, death, displacement, and the bitterness of all kinds of hardship. The number of refugees fleeing to Xiamen has reached 200,000. Although there is a refugee camp on Gulangyu, it is a drop in the ocean and of no avail. The capitalists of Xiamen are still sweeping the snow from their own doorsteps. Recently, the YMCA has stepped forward to establish a reception center, but it is limited to accommodating only 300 people. The majority of refugees are still exposed to the elements, appearing like stray dogs. This miserable situation is still burgeoning, and the Red Peril is expanding daily. Time continues to drag on, and the people of Quanzhou and Xiamen are in constant fear. The cries of the people for help are exhausted and hoarse. Although there are reports of reinforcements being sent from various quarters, they are all empty thunder with no rain. Initially, the Guangdong Army once advanced to the Fujian border, but later, due to internal disputes over the merger of the navy and air force, the troops were recalled. The Guangxi Army's entry into Fujian has been called for repeatedly, but there is still no news of mobilization. Alas, the people of Fujian are suffering and rolling in the depths of water and fire, awaiting death. The homeland of millions of overseas Chinese is about to sink, their family properties have been destroyed, and their relatives are about to die. Those living far overseas are watching such tragic scenes with anguish, unable to find a way to save themselves, and their appeals go unheard. Their hearts are cut like a knife, and they want to cry but have no tears. Party and government officials, in every sentence, call overseas Chinese the mother of the revolution and encourage them to return to the country to start businesses, which is a government policy. Yet, they are now allowing the hometowns of overseas Chinese to be shattered to this extent. Therefore, I only hope that we Fujianese, especially my millions of Fujianese overseas Chinese, will consider how we can save our hometowns in the future. Like a doctor treating a disease, we must first understand the source of the illness, and then prescribe the right medicine to have any hope of bringing back the dead.

Today's Red Peril in Fujian has become a prairie fire. The direct sowers of the seeds of disaster are the various garrison units disguised as bandits, such as the former Gao Yi, Guo Fengming, Wu Wei, and Yang Hanlie, and the current Lu Xingbang, Lin Shouguo, Chen Guohui, Lin Zhong, and the troops of Zhang Zhen, who is known as the commander of the 49th National Revolutionary Army. Indirectly, it is the foolish and incompetent Fujian Provincial Government of the Naval faction. And the former central authorities must also bear responsibility for this situation. I will now delve into this issue.

(1) The Various Garrison Units in Fujian are the Cause of the Red Bandits

After the Northern Expeditionary Army departed from Fujian Province, Tan Shuqing was left behind in Fujian. He incorporated all the bandits who were normally despised by the people, calling them the Newly Organized First Army. At that time, Gao Yi, Wu Wei, Lu Xingbang, Guo Fengming, Chen Guohui, Gao Wei, Yang Hanlie, Ye Dingguo, Wang Hanmin, You Sifu, and others were all division commanders, brigade commanders, and regimental commanders. The people of Fujian, unable to endure their devastation and exploitation, rose up in opposition and appealed for help. Finally, in the winter of 1927, the Eleventh Army (now the 19th Route Army) entered Fujian and violently resolved the Newly Organized Army. At that time, Gao Yi and Yang Hanlie (Wu Wei had already died, and his troops were under Gao Yi) were disarmed in the province. However, Ye Dingguo's unit tried to flee back to their old lair in Tongan, but was completely disarmed by the people of Huyang along the way. Chen Guohui had been transferred to Longyan in advance, and Guo Fengming fled from Quanzhou back to Tingzhou and Yongding. Unfortunately, they could not be rounded up in one fell swoop. In less than two months, the Eleventh Army returned to Guangdong, and the Marine Corps filled the defenses of Quanzhou and Zhangzhou. Soon after, Zhang Zhen's troops also returned to Fujian from Jiangshan County in Zhejiang. The Navy handed over the defense of Zhangzhou to Zhang Zhen. Initially, the people of southern Fujian held a warm hope for Zhang Zhen's return to Fujian, hoping that he could continue the Eleventh Army's thorough work of clearing bandits. Unexpectedly, after arriving in Zhangzhou, he acted contrary to the wishes of the people and did his best to incorporate large and small groups of bandits to expand his own power. Although the people fiercely opposed him, he stubbornly persisted and ignored them. Miscellaneous taxes and levies were increased again. Therefore, the people of Zhangzhou had a folk song that said, "Zhang Yi changed to Zhang Zhen, miscellaneous levies increased by two sheng, regardless of the people's suffering, exclusively recruiting bandit soldiers." This is enough to show the people's sentiment. The counties of Quanzhou and Yongchun were still garrisoned by the Second Brigade of the Marine Corps under Lin Shouguo, who competed to incorporate the bandits Wang Lianming and Gao Weiguo, condoning their rampant extortion, looting, arson, and murder. The people of Jinjiang, Nan'an, and Hui'an were in deep water and fire, while he sat by and shared the spoils. At the same time, Chen Guohui in Longyan and Guo Fengming in Tingzhou and Yongding were even more capable of extreme exploitation and killing. Those who slightly opposed them in Longyan and Tingzhou were repeatedly killed. At that time, Xie Baoxuan, a member of the Longyan County Party Committee, Chen Xueqin, a commissioner, and a member of the Tingzhou Party Committee (whose name I have forgotten), were all brutally murdered for opposing Chen and Guo. Therefore, in the area of western Fujian, all young people with intellectual backgrounds could not gain a foothold, and a large number of them joined the Communist Party. It can truly be said that "driving fish into the deep, driving birds into the thicket." Thus, the Red Peril in western Fujian arose in 1928. Guo Fengming himself was buried in the new tomb he had dug himself, and his entire force was wiped out by the Red Army. The Red Army took advantage of the situation to attack Chen Guohui in Longyan. This time, Chen's troops suffered heavy losses. However, at that time, the Red Army's strength was not yet strong enough, and it temporarily subsided. After Chen Guohui learned this lesson, not only did he not repent, but he became even more tyrannical and reckless, which led to the Red Army's second attack on Longyan in the spring and summer of 1929. This time, Chen Guohui was almost completely wiped out. He escaped to Tongan and concentrated his remaining three or four hundred men. He himself was almost killed. Longyan was lost, and the area of western Fujian became a red world. Subsequently, the provincial government issued an order to suppress Chen. The incident of Lu Xingbang detaining the provincial government committee members occurred. Chen's bandits were then re-incorporated by Fang Shengtao and given the title of Provincial Defense Army. Before long, they were stationed in Quanzhou and Yongchun, appearing as if they were solely responsible for one area. They colluded with Zhang Zhen and acted recklessly, wantonly extorting and exploiting the people. Last winter, they became even more audacious, blatantly forcing the planting of opium seedlings and collecting opium seedling donations. Zhang Zhen actually collected seven or eight million yuan in the counties of Zhangzhou and Tongan, while Chen Guohui actually collected six or seven million yuan in Quanzhou and Yongchun. When the operating expenses and the pockets of the contractors are added together, the total is no less than 20 million yuan. If the counties of Zhangzhou, Quanzhou, and Yongchun have been bled dry year after year to the point of poverty and destitution, how can they withstand such an extreme and insatiable squeeze? Now, the military officers of Zhang and Chen, from battalion commanders and above, have accumulated tens of thousands to millions of yuan in wealth from the people's fat and blood. Therefore, it has also aroused the Red bandits' covetousness, and they have launched a large-scale invasion. At this time, the military officers of Zhang's troops, in order to protect their lives and property, fled at the first sign of trouble. When they withdrew from Zhangzhou, they used a large number of porters to transport opium and cash, while the most needed guns and ammunition for military use were burned to the ground. Since Zhangzhou has fallen, the heavy losses it has suffered are well-deserved. However, the people of Zhanglong have suffered a terrible ravaging, and even hundreds of lives cannot atone for the crimes. In short, if it were not for the brutality and exploitation of Guo Fengming and Chen Guohui, there would be no Red Peril in western Fujian. If it were not for Zhang Zhen's corruption and greed, there would be no tragic situation in Zhangzhou today. Therefore, I say that the cause of the Red Peril in Fujian is these garrison units disguised as bandits, and I have not wronged them in the slightest. (To be continued)

Henan, Hubei, and Anhui Suppress Bandits in Three Routes 76

Chiang Concurrently Leads the Central Route, He and Li Take Charge of the Left and Right Wings

Liu Zhi Arrives in Hankou from Henan to Seek Instructions

Hankou Correspondence: After arriving in Hankou, Chiang Kai-shek, the Commander-in-Chief of the Bandit Suppression in the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, began working at the headquarters on the 29th. On the 30th, he summoned the generals for talks and finalized the overall military plan for bandit suppression. At the same time, he announced the commanders and deputy commanders for the three routes of bandit suppression. On that day, Chiang arrived at the headquarters at 9:00 AM and successively received Zhang Yinxiang, the commander of the 30th Army, He Jingwu, the director of the Ping-Han Railway Bureau, Zhang Zhenhan, the commander of the 41st Division, Xiao Zhichu, the commander of the 44th Division, Rong Jingfang, the commander of the 82nd Division, Tang Enbo, the commander of the 89th Division, Yu Jishi, the commander of the 88th Division, Liu Peixu, the commander of the 37th Independent Brigade, Pan Shanzhai, the commander of the 38th Brigade, and Jiang Zuojun, the commander of the 3rd New Brigade, etc. After individual talks, he assembled them for instructions, mainly stating that in recent years, the bandit forces in the central provinces have become increasingly rampant, and the people have been living in misery. Last year, there was a flood, followed by the Shandong and Tianjin-Shanghai incidents, and the bandit forces became even more rampant, increasing the suffering of the people. Now, bandit suppression has become an urgent task related to the survival of the Party and the nation, and is of utmost importance. He, Chiang, was ordered to come to Hankou and was determined to exert the greatest effort to eliminate the scourge for the people. All officers shared the military responsibility and should use their best efforts to complete the mission. If the Red bandits were not cleared, there would be no way to answer to the Party, the nation, the people, the leader, and the martyrs, and no way to answer to themselves. He, Chiang, had long understood the hard work and struggle of the comrades in the past and hoped that everyone would pay attention to two points in the future: (1) Rectify military discipline and cooperate with the people. Strict military discipline will make the effectiveness even more substantial. With the support of the people, the bandits and communists can be more easily eliminated. (2) Obey the orders of superiors. The situation in Wuhan is complex, and attacks and rumors can be seen at any time. Everyone should recognize that those who attack their comrades and superiors are attacking themselves and must work together under the leadership of their officers to eliminate the great scourge of the Party and the nation, so that the people can have permanent peace. He also hoped that all comrades would respect the Party and its doctrines and policies so that they can be realized. After the instructions, Chiang returned to the Yihua Village residence and ordered the adjutant's office and the Supervisory Office to notify the following personnel to attend the hearing at the appointed time: on July 1st, members of the Provincial Party Headquarters and the Hankou Special City Party Headquarters; on the 2nd, members of the Hubei Provincial Government and the heads of various departments; on the 4th, regimental commanders and above of the Ping-Han Railway (Southern Section) and the troops stationed in Wuhan would be summoned for instructions; and the Provincial Government would be ordered to telegraph all county magistrates to attend the provincial meeting and summoned for instructions before July 10th. That night, Chiang decided to divide the bandit suppression into three routes. The central route was along the Ping-Han Railway, with Chiang concurrently serving as the commander and Liu Zhi as the deputy commander; the right route was along the Jinpu Railway, with Li Jishen as the commander and Wang Jun as the deputy commander; and the left route was in the counties of central Hubei, with He Chengjun as the commander and Xu Yuanquan as the deputy commander. Below the commander, there would be a column commander, and the candidates had been decided internally but not announced. After the deployment was determined, the Pacification Commissioners, Commanders-in-Chief, Commanders of Armies, Divisions and Brigades, and Commanders of Various Commands were instructed that in the future, without orders, they were not allowed to leave their defense areas without permission and come to Hankou casually. Those in Hankou were required to return to their defense areas by July 1st. Until 9:00 PM, Chiang hosted a banquet for Navy Commander Zeng Yiding and the captains of the various ships, and also hosted Li Yuying and his wife, who had just arrived in Hankou from Nanjing. The arrangements for Lojia Mountain were originally prepared by the Provincial Government for Chiang's temporary residence, but due to the pressing military affairs, the trip may be cancelled. It is rumored that the future residence has been chosen as Jigong Mountain, and the director of the Ping-Han Railway Bureau has telegraphed the stationmaster to arrange Jin Yun'e's residence. The date of departure has not yet been decided.

Liu Zhi, Chairman of the Henan Provincial Government and Pacification Commissioner stationed in Henan, personally led the First, Second, and Thirty-third Divisions to Minggang to supervise the bandit suppression due to the bandit alarm on the Ping-Han Railway. Now that the bandits have been routed and the entire railway has been repaired and opened to traffic, he accompanied Jiang Chu'ou, the commander of the railway artillery team, south by train on the 30th. They arrived at 12:00 PM that night and met with Chiang in the morning of the 1st to report on the progress of bandit suppression and seek instructions. It is also heard that He Chengjun will go to Shashi within a few days to inspect the 21st Army, represent Chiang Kai-shek to offer condolences, and return in one or two days, then go to various counties in the central Hubei area to inspect and cooperate with Xu Yuanquan in supervising the suppression of the Red bandits. (June 30th)

Chiang Orders the Provincial Government of Hubei to Supervise Han Yucheng 77

Because Han Has Remarks Discrediting the Kuomintang

Hankou Correspondence: After Xia Douyin took office as the Chairman of the Hubei Provincial Government, he specially established the Provincial Administration Design Committee, employing more than 50 scholars and celebrities to discuss and deliberate on civil affairs, finance, construction, and education, preparing for government adoption and consultation. The committee was formally established on June 25. One of the members, Han Yucheng, a former National Assembly member from the Politics Studies Clique, gave a speech at the conference, in which he said, "In the past, the Kuomintang did not allow the people to speak. The Kuomintang members are too uncultured. They have no solutions themselves and do not allow others to have solutions, leading to bandits everywhere, harming the country and the people. This is all the root of the disaster left by Sun Yat-sen. Now the Kuomintang is not responsible. They can only destroy, and they want us engineers to build. We look at it inside the house and think it is very good, but the countryside is full of murder and arson, and the people are living in misery. The cities are extravagant and dissolute, and the powerful officials are tyrannical. The Kuomintang's proposition, only the eight characters of loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, faith, righteousness, harmony, and peace are correct, but this is also our proposition for many years." As soon as the speech was finished, there was a reaction in the hall. A faction of committee members questioned the reasons, and some even demanded that Han leave the meeting, but there were also those who defended Han. The two sides debated for a long time. The next day, committee members Qiu Bohang and others reported to the provincial and municipal party headquarters. Both party headquarters believed that Han's remarks were discrediting the Kuomintang and insulting the Kuomintang leader. Therefore, they convened a temporary emergency meeting on the 29th and decided to ask the provincial government to remove Han from his position. At the same time, they sent a letter to the bandit suppression headquarters of the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, and the Hubei Pacification Commissioner's Office, requesting them to arrest him strictly, and said that most of the design committee members were corrupt and evil elements, and decided to request its cancellation. After hearing the news, Han sent a letter to Xia Douyin and the members of the provincial government on the 30th, saying, "My colleagues recommended me to give a speech. Touched by the scene, I repeatedly sighed at the instability of people's hearts and the degeneration of the world. This heart and this will can swear to heaven and earth. Unexpectedly, the virtuous ones in the party have misunderstood. I have exhausted my foolish sincerity, but it has brought the burden of great fame. I earnestly request permission to dismiss my position as a design committee member, so as to avoid blame." Attached to the letter was the speech record of the day.

The above-mentioned remarks considered reactionary have not been deleted, but the meaning is more euphemistic, the theory is deeper, and the logic is more comprehensive. Attached is Han Yucheng's own record of his speech: "Today, the officials and gentry of Hubei gather together to sit and discuss the reforms of Hubei. I am very pleased. In the past six years, the National Government and local governments did not allow the common people to speak about political facilities. Now the gentlemen of the Hubei Provincial Government are humbly seeking advice from everyone about the design of the provincial administration. Their broad minds are really admirable. Chairman Xia just said that we should seek construction for the welfare of the people, of course, including farmland, water conservancy, industry, commerce, and mutual assistance. I would like to add one more point: material design is important, but how to design the spiritual, which is invisible and formless? That is, the so-called cultivation. All achievements flow from cultivation. Only with great and magnificent cultivation can there be great and magnificent achievements. Tranquility leads to far-sightedness, and what is inside manifests outside. This is an unchanging principle of ancient and modern times. The policy plans of the National Government often change and often shake. The laws and regulations announced by various agencies are like hairs. What was right yesterday is wrong today, and the country is at a loss, resulting in the loss of the center of gravity of politics and society. The world is in turmoil and cannot be governed. The reason for this is that it places too much emphasis on material design and neglects the spiritual aspect. Therefore, it is sometimes slow and sometimes urgent, sometimes left and sometimes right, and there is no fixed direction for reforms. The frequent changes of those in power are a major reason, but the wavering of spirit is the main reason. Spiritual instability will inevitably lead to a lack of mastery in the heart. A lack of mastery in the heart will inevitably lead to a shift with the environment, unable to control the environment. Therefore, those who quelled great turmoil and cleared thorns in the past did not necessarily make rituals and music or lay out tracks, because the principles of ceremonies, cultures, and plans for governing the country are profound and the matters are extensive, which cannot be handled in a rush of war. In the times of Wen Jing and Kang Qian, many people of the past dynasties or hermits in the mountains and forests were sought to fill the task of making laws, probably because their minds were clear and their cultivation was pure, so they were always successful. Otherwise, if one relies solely on material design, thinking that it can benefit the country and the people, look at the Krupp factory in front of us. Its design can be said to be complete, but because it is obsessed with military power and force, it has evolved into an unprecedented tragedy in Europe, and as for the country being broken and the family destroyed, it has become a laughingstock in the world. What is the value of the Krupp factory? Mr. Zhongshan's eight-character training says: Loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, faith, righteousness, harmony, and peace. This is truly a priceless plan for our spiritual cultivation. All material designs must be produced from these eight characters to be truly called design. One can win the world on horseback, but one cannot govern the world on horseback, which is the principle of emphasizing both strength and virtue, rectifying people's hearts to rectify the world, and cultivating oneself to pacify the people. It sounds very common, but it is indeed not easy to do. Look at the surroundings outside the auditorium. What is the scene? Everywhere there is murder and arson, making everyone unable to live in peace, and even having to join the bandits, because the spirit is frantic and involuntary, and the inner heart loses the power of control, and many evils outside are born from this. We should all bear the mission of transforming people's hearts and strengthening the spirit, and do it step by step. Therefore, after Chairman Xia's speech, I would like to add one more point, and I hope you will forgive my arrogance." (June 30)

The Mystery of the Northeast K 79

(3) The Key to Creating the Greatest Necessity on the New Continent (1) The Northeast, which is about the size of Germany and France combined, was occupied by the Japanese army in less than three days. There are naturally many reasons for this ease, but the transportation agencies, especially the railways, have long been controlled by the Japanese, which cannot be denied as the most relevant fact. Therefore, to study the Northeast issue, we must take the railway as the backbone.

Using economic means to destroy a country is the most wonderful way to kill people without bloodshed. Isn't today's South Manchuria Railway Company the incarnation of the former East India Company? For the past twenty-five years, the power of the South Manchuria Railway Company has been deeply rooted in the Northeast. The Manchuria-Mongolia New Five Routes are the branches and leaves that have grown from this main line. The Japanese hope to blossom and bear fruit there every day, realizing the so-called "Third Phase of the Meiji Emperor's Plan," to conquer China by destroying Manchuria and Mongolia, and to conquer Asia and the world by destroying China.

(2) From the phrase "South Manchuria State," one can imagine the magnitude of the South Manchuria Railway Company's business scope. In addition to its own business, it includes mining, iron smelting, oil refining, port construction, shipbuilding, warehousing, hotels, shipping, industry, electricity, gas, and even geological surveys, agricultural experiments, veterinary research, urban management, sanitation, education, security, water supply, industry, commerce, and various facilities, almost all-inclusive. From an organizational point of view, the Japanese can control the Northeast, and it is more appropriate to say that it is the success of the South Manchuria Railway Company than the success of soldiers and vagrants.

The purpose of the South Manchuria Railway Company has now been largely achieved, but in order to further expand its business scope, it has decided to increase its capital by 360 million yuan to become 800 million yuan. In October of this year, 20 million yuan will be collected first for the use of new projects, and the remainder will be raised in ten years or less, depending on the urgency of the need.

The new projects of the South Manchuria Railway Company that have been announced include the following:

(1) In order to develop Manchuria and Mongolia, the company's Economic Committee will cooperate with the Japanese government to conduct an economic survey of the resources of Manchuria and Mongolia.

(2) In order to avoid public attention, the company's affiliated businesses and various affiliated companies, such as South Manchuria Gas Co., Ltd., South Manchuria Electric Co., Ltd., Dalian Industry Co., Ltd., South Manchuria Hotel Co., Ltd., Manchuria Shipyard Co., Ltd., Fushun Coal Sales Co., Ltd., Dalian Steamship Co., Ltd., and Fuchang Labor Co., Ltd., will be formed into a special company to make them independent.

(3) In order to revitalize the Manchuria-Mongolia trade with Japan, in addition to the trade halls that have been established in Jinzhou, Jilin, Dunhua, Harbin, Sanxing, Qiqihar, and Ning'an, it has been decided to add trade halls in Fuyu, Taonan, and other places.

The Japanese government, imitating the precedent of annexing Korea, intends to establish a Manchuria Governor-General to unify the political power of the Northeast. Therefore, the various benefits granted to the South Manchuria Railway Company in the past must be greatly weakened and changed into a purely commercial agency. The president of the company, Yasuya Uchida, has been appointed as the Minister of Foreign Affairs, and this plan will probably be realized soon, and Uchida's advocacy of recognizing the puppet state is what we should pay attention to.

(3) After the September 18 Incident, regarding the railway, the Japanese first took over the Northeast Transportation Committee, appointing Ding Jianxiu as the chairman. If any employees of each route resigned, they were replaced by Japanese. Otherwise, Japanese employees were added. At first, they were called counselors, but later they felt that there was no basis, so they changed to the name of liaison officer "trustee." They intervened in everything, large and small. Later, the puppet Ministry of Transportation was established, and Ding was still appointed as the puppet minister. The Northeast Transportation Committee was abolished on March 25.

The puppet Ministry of Transportation has four divisions: General Affairs, Railway, Postal Affairs, and Water Transportation. The Director of the General Affairs Division is Okayika Chikao, the Director of the Railway Division is Shigeyuki Morita, and the Director of the Postal Affairs Division is Yasuaki Fujita. Okayika Chikao is the stationmaster of the South Manchuria Railway Changchun Station. It is conceivable that the ministry's affairs are entirely in the hands of the Japanese.

The puppet Railway Division is divided into General Affairs, Road Works, Management, and the First to Fifth Sections. The First Section manages the Jichang, Jidun, and Jihai lines, the Second Section manages the Sitao, Taoang, and Qike lines, the Third Section manages the Fengshan and Panhai lines, the Fourth Section manages the Huhai line, and the Fifth Section manages the Chinese Eastern Railway. The organization is extremely peculiar.

After the establishment of the puppet Ministry of Transportation, it held the so-called "National Railway Conference" on May 1. The issues discussed were roughly as follows:

(1) Improving the joint transportation methods and unifying the timetable of the Fengshan, Shenhai, Jihai, Jidun, Jichang, Chinese Eastern, Taoang, Sitao, and Qike lines.

(2) Rectifying the waiting rooms of each station and increasing all facilities.

(3) Improving the hotels and restaurants at each station and the vending departments in the cars.

(4) Expanding the road protection guard and increasing the road police accompanying the car.

(5) Arranging the seats in each train and paying attention to the hygiene in the car.

(6) Cracking down on road staff and foot traffic, and not allowing them to deceive passengers and demand extra money.

In order to prevent attacks by volunteer troops and bandits, the Japanese stipulated that photography is not allowed in the railway area, and tall crops such as sorghum and corn are not allowed to be planted within 1,600 feet on both sides of the railway. Miscellaneous people are not allowed to stay on the platform. In the past, the roads promoted tree planting, and looking out from the car, the green and blue were intertwined. Today, the Japanese are afraid that volunteer troops or bandits are hiding in them, so they have cut down almost all of them, turning them into barren scenes, which can be said to be a great disappointment.

In order to thoroughly control the road affairs, in addition to transferring students from the South Manchuria Railway Training Institute, a car service training school was set up to train low-level road staff, and a police officer school was set up to train road protection leaders. In addition, because the train telegraphs on each route are now changed to Japanese, a sound machine training school was specially set up to train station announcers. The lecturers are all hired by the South Manchuria Railway Company, and the salaries are extremely high. It is also foreseeable that the Northeast road affairs will be completely Japanized.

The various routes in the Northeast used to collect educational surcharges for supplementary education, and there were regulations on discounted fares for immigrants and free transportation of agricultural tools to promote colonization. Now, all of these have been cancelled by the Japanese, which shows that the Japanese only implement their due policies and do not care about the interests of others. (To be continued)

Songjiang 81

The Construction Bureau Strictly Controls Construction in Townships: The construction control in the urban area of the county has been implemented long ago, but it has not been possible to send personnel to handle the construction in the distant townships. A Homicide Occurred in Dongqiao: Zhang, the wife of Zhu Xiaobao, a farmer in Dongqiao Township, was 45 years old. She had an affair with the long-term worker Ma Shuijin. The next day, the township spread the rumor that Dong had been beaten to death by her aunt Zhang, and that Ma Shuijin had been paid forty yuan to bury Dong's body in the bamboo garden. Changzhou 83

The Case of Killing Police Officers and Police: Four bandits were drinking tea at the Longquan Teahouse (mistakenly reported as Ruyi Teahouse yesterday) near the Nan Yun Bridge outside the Ximen of Wuyi at 7 a.m. on the 30th. After being secretly reported, Assistant Officer Zhao Wei led the police to arrest them. Unexpectedly, the bandits opened fire and resisted arrest, shooting and wounding Zhao Wei and the police officer Hou Jichun on the spot, who died one after another. The bandits immediately fired their guns all the way and fled to Xicang Bridge, where they shot and wounded a police officer, Li Dianyi. At 6:20 p.m., Li died of his injuries. After being examined by the court prosecutor, the coffins of the three were all parked at Guangfu Temple outside Ximen for a memorial service in the future. Officer Zhao Wei was scheduled to be buried at 10 a.m. today (1st). After the bandits escaped, Chief Fang of the Public Security Bureau telegraphed the waterway and land police forces and ordered all bureaus to strictly arrest the perpetrators. At 10 a.m. on the same day, the bandit Wu Yuhai (from Shantou, Guangdong) was arrested half a mile west of Lianjiang Bridge west of Xinzha. At 12 p.m., the Qishuyan police force intercepted Zhang Zikun (from Guangxi) and Yang Yan (from Jiangxi) near Dingyan Pingqiao. When Zhang and Yang were captured, they were sitting in rickshaws. All three were soldiers. They were escorted to the Public Security Bureau that night and questioned by Chief Fang. Wu Yumei confessed that Zhang fired the gun at Longquan Teahouse, while Zhang's confession was vague, only admitting that he was eating tea with Yang upstairs. The shooting was done by the companions who escaped. The three criminals were ordered to be detained temporarily. In the deep night, the owners of the Changfa and Changxing inns where the criminals were hiding were also interrogated. It was also heard that a total of three police officers died in this battle. Officer Zhao Wei was 29 years old, a local, and had not yet married. Officer Hou Jichun was 23 years old, from Henan. Li Dianyi was 37 years old, from Beiping. They died heroically in this anti-burglary act.

Wuxi 84

A Shocking Report of Human Life Killed by Feces and Filth: Wu Yunxiang, a resident of Luoshe Town, Wanan City, the 16th district of the county, worked as a train guard. He married a wife, Qiang, who was beautiful but extremely fierce. Therefore, the villagers called her "Sai Daji." Yunxiang had a younger brother named Shengxiang, who worked in Zhejiang. He married a wife, Ding, who was gentle. Qiang saw that she was weak and often bullied her. On the afternoon of the 27th of last month, Ding went out for something and returned home, and saw that the waist door was slightly ajar. When she reached the room, she noticed that three chests and cages were missing. She immediately questioned Yunxiang, saying that he should not have left the waist door ajar, causing the thief to visit and suffer this loss. Before she could finish speaking, she provoked Qiang's anger. Qiang immediately instigated Yunxiang to beat and poison Ding severely, and forcibly poured waste matter into Ding's stomach. Because Ding closed her lips tightly, they used sewing needles to stab her lips randomly. Immediately, blood flowed like a torrent, and her breathing was short. Then, she fainted and became unconscious. By the afternoon of the 30th of last month, she died of serious injuries. After hearing the news, Ding's father was extremely sad and indignant. In addition to urgently telegraphing Ding's husband, Wu Shengxiang, to return to his hometown, he went to the county court yesterday with the various chiefs to report and request an examination to redress the injustice. However, Yunxiang and his wife had already carried 100 yuan in silver and 4 dou of white rice when Ding was critically ill and absconded without a trace in the deep night.

Danyang 85

Northeast Township Robbery and Injury Case: The home of Xu Jinhua in Xujia Village, Lucheng, was suddenly visited by many bandits with sharp weapons last night, who broke into the door and searched wildly. Not satisfied with what they had, they burned the mother of the person in charge. The home of Jiang Yinsheng in Yongning Township was also visited by more than a dozen bandits yesterday, who turned over the house and imprisoned the old and young of the Yinsheng family in a room, searching at will. They then invaded and looted the neighboring home of Jiang Gui, and seized the mother of the township chief Jiang Jiaji, and forced her to hand over money. Failing to do so, they burned her with fire. The flesh and blood were charred and unbearably painful to look at. The case has been reported and an arrest is requested.

A Plague is Rampant in the City: Recently, the weather has been bad, and true cholera has been discovered in the city of this county, and it is coming very fiercely. More than ten people have died before they could be treated. Zou Wuzhi, the chief of the Public Security Bureau, specially submitted a request to the county government to establish a summer epidemic prevention center, and hired a Western doctor to administer free preventive injections, and also instructed the police chiefs to add to the propaganda, in order to awaken the people's attention to hygiene.

Central University Continues Classes Amid Calls for Dissolution 88

How to Handle the Ministry of Education's Order to Dissolve Awaits Instructions

Elected Members of the School Protection Committee Declare They Will Not Take Office

Central University, due to students assaulting Duan Xipeng, was resolved by the Executive Yuan to temporarily dissolve Central University and reorganize it separately. In addition to receiving three telegrams of condolence to Duan Xipeng from the Ministry of Education on the 30th, (Wang Jingqi's telegram said, "I was shocked by your suffering yesterday, and I am very concerned. Please telegraph the details."), the Ministry of Education will await the instructions of the Executive Yuan meeting on the 1st regarding how to deal with Central University, and will follow the order to handle it. The professors at Central University have expressed no opinion. The students continued to attend classes as usual on the 30th. However, the members of the School Protection Movement Committee elected at the plenary meeting on the 29th, Zhou Richao, Zhang Chubao, Chen Wusheng, Wang Feng, Chang Lun, Qu Bochuan, Jiang Jie, Xie Yizhen, Yan Zhongrui, Chen Kejie, and Hu Jibang, jointly declared: "We hereby inform you that after the Duan incident on the 28th, we were elected by the plenary meeting as members of the School Protection Movement Committee and stipulated the working principles to solve the two problems of the president and funding. However, the Executive Yuan suddenly made a decision to dissolve the school on the same day. Since this matter is of great importance and exceeds the scope of the working principles, we cannot take office. We hereby declare."

Notes from an Old Temple Bell (40) 92

— Zhai Fu, who doesn't remove the courtyard grass

44. Why did Mr. Zhu rush into the city like that? This is quite a guess. But I firmly believe that Mr. Zhu will definitely come back. He didn't bring his little brother into the city with him, how could he not come back?

Sure enough, in the red light of the setting sun, Mr. Zhu came back, and we were overjoyed. Mr. Zhu also had a friend with him. Through his introduction, we knew that this friend was a retired military officer.

Mr. Zhu said, "Zhong'er! Go to the village and greet everyone, saying that I have a good way to prevent bandits. Anyone who has a gun at home, please come to the meeting with your gun when you hear the bell." What a good news this is! The village couldn't wait for me to ring the bell, and everyone came rushing without even having dinner. Those with guns came proudly, and those without guns also came to join the fun. I was wrong, they didn't come to join the fun, but to know how to prevent bandits! In fact, I didn't need to ring the bell to gather everyone, because everyone had already arrived before the bell was rung. But I had to ring the bell as promised. Strange! Tonight's bell sound is particularly loud, which makes people feel a hundred times more courageous.

The main hall couldn't accommodate everyone, so we had to gather on the open space in front of the ancient temple. Mr. Zhu said, "I have considerable sympathy for the heroes forced to go to Liangshan. But even being a robber should have a reason. Robbers who kill children are unprincipled robbers. Children are our God, and we must fight against robbers who kill children. The robbers may come tonight! The child they want to kidnap may be the baby you are holding in your arms. There is only one way to prevent the robbers from coming. Those with guns should unite and obey a commander-in-chief for emergency combat! I have invited my friend Battalion Commander Jiang to teach you. We don't want to learn the military formalism of standing at attention, marching, and turning around. What Battalion Commander Jiang wants to teach you is how to fight in a battle. Suppose robbers come to kidnap our children at 10:00 tonight, or imperialists come to dig up our ancestors' graves and seize our beautiful mountains and rivers, how should we learn in these three or four hours to resist one against a hundred? Good, let's learn to defeat imperialism by defeating the robbers. Now, please ask Battalion Commander Jiang for guidance."

Battalion Commander Jiang: "I don't want to teach military formalism, and I don't want to say polite words. There are four hours left before the robbers come, what should we do? (1) Light up torches to learn target practice. Everyone should first learn to aim and take turns firing three bullets. If there are few bullets, firing one bullet is also acceptable. (2) Learn to load and disassemble guns. (3) Learn emergency assembly. (4) Divide those with guns into two teams, one team playing robbers, and the other team playing the self-defense group, learning offensive and defensive field battles."

Battalion Commander Jiang said and immediately lit torches to start. After learning the four items that night, guards were assigned to take turns guarding the night. The password is the two characters "Yue Fei." Those who don't know the password cannot pass. Thus, the entire village entered a state of martial law. Every strong man became a selfless warrior, and the kind of fearful and uneasy terror that was once felt had long disappeared.

A Pitiable Reflection on the Past and Present of Shanghai's Chinese Baseball 95

Once Won Two National Championships, But Where is the Glory Now?

Now There are Comets Appearing, the Sports Association Should Vigorously Sponsor Them

Shanghai is the center of sports in our country. Various sports have their own special spirit and strong interest. However, baseball, lacking promotion and practice, is declining, and there is a trend of extinction. The reason is that there is a lack of funds and talent, and those who are responsible for promotion also take it lightly and do not encourage it. In the past few years, occasionally several people went to the China Baseball Field to practice, but due to their immature skills and lack of encouragement, they disappeared.

Recalling the past of the Shanghai baseball community, there were considerable achievements. In 1926, the National Regional Baseball Championship was held. At that time, the South China team was unable to attend due to an incident. Only the North China and East China teams competed in Shanghai for the championship. As a result, East China won two consecutive games and won the championship. Since then, the interest in baseball in Shanghai has become more and more intense. The public has also gradually paid attention. With the promoters having enthusiasm, the players also felt more and more excited, and the baseball movement saw a vigorous atmosphere.

In the summer of 1928, Shanghai organized the China Baseball Team, recruited talents, and worked hard to train. The skills improved even more than before. They participated in the Shanghai Foreign Baseball League. There were five teams participating. Although the Chinese team could not defeat the Maisner's Races and Paines teams, the wins and losses of each game were often within one or two points. Moreover, they were able to defeat the well-known amateur team and the naval team, ranking third. During the competition, it caused a sensation in Shanghai, and the spectators were enthusiastic. In addition to the foreign league, there was also a junior baseball league, with teams from Chinese Yi, Jewish, American Public School, Shanghai Jiang and John's and Tongwen schools participating. This was the most prosperous time for the baseball community.

In the same year, in addition to participating in the Shanghai Baseball League, the China Baseball Team also led its troops south to Hong Kong at the end of August to compete with the South China team, the originator of baseball in China, in the National Regional Baseball Championship. At that time, the rising Shanghai baseball team surprised everyone and was invincible. The first game with South China ended in a 3-3 tie. Due to the late hour, it could not be finished. South China won the second game with 5-4. Shanghai won the third game with 5-0. Shanghai won the fourth game with 9-5. Thus, they were crowned champions and regained the title of National Baseball Leader. In Hong Kong, they also competed with various strong foreign teams. Shanghai won every game and returned triumphantly.

Shanghai baseball was just beginning to show its potential, and its prospects seemed limitless. Unexpectedly, times changed, and the situation deteriorated day by day. The following year, talents scattered, and strength was greatly reduced. Although a few enthusiastic people shouted loudly, no one responded, resulting in a gradual decline.

In 1930, there was still no new atmosphere. The Sports Advancement Association also gradually became indifferent and did not revitalize it. Last year, Zhang Guoxun, Li Baojun, Liu Dacheng, and other heroes of the Shanghai baseball community shouted loudly, intending to reorganize. They also realized that without a stable organization in the baseball community, it would be difficult to develop the cause. Therefore, they initiated the organization of the Shanghai China Baseball Association to divide into teams for practice and promote skills. At that time, there were fifty or sixty people who joined. The founding meeting was held at the China YMCA on Sichuan Road, and the spirit was quite enthusiastic. However, it soon disappeared invisibly, and there were no achievements to be said. Full of enthusiasm turned into nothing.

As mentioned above, the rise and fall of the Shanghai baseball community is truly regrettable. What can the enthusiastic baseball fans in Shanghai, the sports instructors of various universities, and the Sports Advancement Association do to comfort themselves and others?

Time flies, and the racecourse is full of enthusiastic popularity again. What will happen to our country? The China Baseball Field is covered with green grass, and no one comes. Is it not a pity? The Sports Advancement Association should at least bear a certain responsibility.

In this bleak and deserted Chinese baseball community, two comets have suddenly appeared, with great ambitions, intending to revitalize Shanghai baseball. It is hoped that the Sports Advancement Association and other enthusiastic baseball fans will vigorously sponsor them and work together.

Who are they? They are Liang Fuchu and Liang Chengshong from the Yokohama Chinese Sports Association. This time, they were angered by the violent Japanese invasion of China and returned to the country. They are now living in Shanghai and plan to gather baseball comrades to reorganize the China Baseball Team to promote the cause. Liang Fuchu is nearly forty years old and was the former supervisor and catcher of the Yokohama Chinese Baseball Team. Liang Chengshong is the second baseman and center fielder, both of whom are proficient in this field and enthusiastic about this cause.

The two Liangs will contact famous players in Shanghai such as Zhang Guozhu and Li Baojun to gather the players and organize a team to engage in training. This is truly a ray of dawn for the Shanghai Chinese baseball community. Liang hopes that enthusiastic people will respond and rise up, making the twilight sports community and the dying baseball community like the rising sun in the east, emitting a beautiful and brilliant light. One cannot help but offer heartfelt prayers.

Free Talk

Second-hand art

Lingdingyang 99

—

People fear fame, pigs fear fattening – this is an old saying. In fact, not only do people fear fame, but places also fear fame. A place that is not usually well-known suddenly becomes bustling and lively, which must mean the place has become a war zone! In recent years, Changxindian in the north, Huangdu in the south, and Miaohang, the most resistant to Japan, have all been in the news; however, when a place becomes famous, the people there suffer!

Changxin hardships become a war zone, Huangdu becomes a war zone – these are all historical stains; only the battle of Miaohang is a war against foreigners, a war to preserve the nation, and it carries considerable historical honor.

Lingdingyang, Lingdingyang – although this term is not well-known in the world, it has an enduring memory in the history of the Southern Song Dynasty.

"Since ancient times, who can avoid death? Let me keep a loyal heart shining in the pages of history." Is this not a line from Wen Tianxiang's poem as he passed through Lingdingyang? Wen Tianxiang, holding this loyal heart, wanted to restore the Song Dynasty; his war was a war against foreigners, a war to preserve the nation; these two rousing lines of poetry added much color to Lingdingyang.

Now, war has broken out again in Lingdingyang. Using the planes of our Republic of China to bomb the warships of our Republic of China! The warships are also using the anti-aircraft guns of our Republic of China to shoot down the planes of our Republic of China! Of China's army, navy, and air force, only the army is usable: as for the others, the navy is not a navy, and the air force is not an air force. Patriotic youths are shouting to expand the navy and expand the air force, but unexpectedly these few bits and pieces of the navy and air force still want to play this trick, playing it until they all perish together before they are willing to stop!

The water in Lingdingyang sobbed and said: Wen Tianxiang's honor to us has all been bombed away by this intense gunfire and bombs.

The Spirit of Tseng, Tso, and Peng in Governance 100

— Bicheng

Reports indicate that during the Lushan Conference, Chiang delivered a speech emphasizing the need to change our mindset and emulate the spirit of Tseng, Tso, and Peng in governance to rectify the prevailing atmosphere and strive for improvement. Our nation's malady has reached a critical stage. Prescribing this remedy is undoubtedly appropriate. However, there is a saying in society: "Speaking of a true prescription, selling fake medicine." Even if the prescription is correct, if the medicine is fake, it cannot bring about a revival. Finding a good prescription is still possible, but obtaining genuine medicine is a greater concern. I will now elaborate on the authenticity of the medicine, even if it seems verbose. We must first understand the origin of the spirit of governance possessed by wise and outstanding individuals in the past. It did not solely rely on innate talent. It was the result of cultivation. Firstly, they read ancient books and elucidated the great principles. Secondly, they received instruction from wise fathers and elder brothers at home and earnest counsel from good teachers and friends outside. Thirdly, they regarded all forms of entertainment, wealth, and profit that could bewitch or ensnare them as venomous snakes and fierce tigers, avoiding them as if fearing to be too slow. With sufficient cultivation in these three aspects, upon entering governance, their spirit would naturally be abundant and invigorated because they were wholeheartedly devoted to the public good of the nation and its people, unburdened by selfish desires. Possessing such integrity, their ability to influence would naturally be strong. Their generals and subordinates would encourage themselves. An atmosphere would arise where civil officials did not covet money, and military officers did not fear death. The learning of Tseng, Tso, and Peng can be summarized in one word: diligence. Tseng often said that one should learn from those who surpass oneself and compare one's circumstances with those less fortunate. During his time in the capital, he benefited from a group of Confucian scholars like Wo Genfeng and Feng Shutang, meticulously recording their every word and action in his diary, striving not to deceive himself and rigorously self-improving (as seen in "Tseng Wenzhenggong's Family Letters"). When Tseng recommended Tso, he praised him as being resolute, wise, enduring hardship, and understanding military strategy. When he recommended Peng, he praised him as being steadfast, persevering, and possessing the spirit of ancient martyrs (as seen in "Tseng Wenzhenggong's Major Events"). After Tso's marriage, he lived with his wife's family, but soon sought independence. In his self-authored epitaph for Madam Zhou, he wrote, "Ashamed of not being self-sufficient, I requested a room in my mother-in-law's western house for separate residence" (as seen in "Collected Essays of Dunbi"). Peng's father served as a patrol inspector in a certain county in Zhejiang. He accumulated a modest salary and entrusted a relative to purchase land in Hengyang. After his father's death, the relative embezzled the land. Peng was still young but determined to seek revenge. His mother dissuaded him and encouraged him to be self-reliant through diligence (as seen in "Biography of Madam Wang, Mother of Peng" in "Collected Essays of Dunbi"). These examples demonstrate that their virtues were forged through diligence. The best medicines grow in the mountains, requiring many years to develop deep roots and potent properties. When harvested and used, they are naturally effective. Nowadays, most medicines are planted in shallow soil and quickly grown with fertilizers. They may appear beautiful, even surpassing the materials grown in the mountains over many years. However, when used to treat illnesses, they are found to be ineffective, and the disease becomes incurable. Lately, when I observe worldly affairs, I often think of the saying "Speaking of a true prescription, selling fake medicine" and sigh deeply. Government officials likely have experienced the harm of fake medicine and will hopefully awaken in the future.

Ramblings on Lychees 101

— Zheng Yimei

In the midst of summer, lychees are the most treasured fruit. Their shells resemble red crepe, their membranes are like purple silk, their flesh is like white fat, and their sweetness is like sweet wine. No wonder a concubine smiled brightly at the sight of a rider bearing them through the red dust. A guest who was familiar with lychee varieties described several names, all with exquisite taste. Some lychees are named for their similar fragrance, such as "Hundred-Step Orchid" and "Musk Box." Some are named for their similar shape, such as "Ox Heart," "Ark Shell," "Scarlet Persimmon," "Tiger Thorn," and "Pine and Cypress Fortress." Some are named for their season, such as "Half-Ripe," for its lovely crimson color. Among the red varieties are "Square Red," "Official Red," "First-Rank Red," "Tortoiseshell Red," "Top Scholar Red," "Household Manager Red," "Zhou Family Red," "He Family Red," "Autumn Champion Red," "Double Seventh Red," "Star Ball Red," and "Longevity Red." For their pleasing green hue, the green varieties are named "River Green," "Green Leaf Fragrance," "Green Kernel," "Mid-Autumn Green," and "Green Robe." Others, such as "You Family Bundle," "French White Stone," "Large Wax," and "Small Wax," display magnificent colors. Volcanic lychees come from Southern Yue, and Fengting Post lychees come from Xinghua, both known as superior varieties. Those that ripen in June are called "June Honey," and those whose flesh resembles crystal are called "Crystal Kingdom." Those that hang in pairs are called "Hui Garden," and those with tiny kernels are called "Burnt Kernel." Other names include "Phoenix Offering," "Dragon Contending Jar," "Forget-the-Child," "Hairpin Bead," "Eighteen Maiden," "Large Eggplant," "Double Silk," "Golden Thread," and "Chicken Leading Child," totaling seventy-five varieties, too numerous to list. I said, "Hearing your talk for one evening is better than tasting ten thousand lychees." The guest smiled. Tonight, I hastily write this.

Restore the Pre-January 28th Status! 102

— Long Sao

During the day, one cannot see horse-drawn carriages fully loaded with bedding; at night, one cannot hear the roaring of murderous sounds cutting through the sky. The music and images of a city filled with terror and turmoil no longer enter the eyes or stir the hearts of everyone. Everything has returned to a peaceful Shanghai, having washed away the blood and swallowed the tears. Even the broken walls and rubble of Zhabei and the desolate wastelands of Wusong are now separated into another century. All the silver cafes of mysterious arts are again filled with proud youths, and the sounds of leather boots and pairs of black shadows have increased on the sidewalks where the moonlight flows like cream.

In the grassy fragrance of the slanting setting sun, on the green lawns of the parks once trod upon by wooden clogs, Chinese young gentlemen and fleshy misses linger, gazing into each other's eyes and touching lips. How can falling leaves disturb their rosy dreams?

In white houses surrounded by night, there are black-haired heads moving in the reflection of the screen, and the songs of the amusement parks generally have a large clientele who know how to appreciate them. Cars on the roads, foreign money in the shops, and even the Eastern Bookstore have all returned to the state before January 28th.

Therefore, must we thank the Shanghai Ceasefire Agreement for giving us such great comfort and the selfish pleasures of every habit?

The demon of war has fled, followed by our own search for good fortune to indulge ourselves. What a "good fortune" it is, leading us into a forever-deepening dream, while awaiting the coming of another war in which we are bullied because we cannot save ourselves!

A curse on the wisdom of the Shanghai people!

Prevention of Epidemics 103

— Chi Fo

The plum rains drip, and new moss grows on the walls. It is midsummer. Epidemics are heard of in Shanghai. Since the Battle of Shanghai, the dead have piled up. Lao Tzu said, "After a great army, there will surely be a year of famine." Indeed, war is a fierce and dangerous thing. With many corpses accumulating, epidemics arise from this. After the Taiping Rebellion in the late Qing Dynasty, epidemics were rampant in the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. After the rebellion in Hunan the year before last, epidemics also occurred, with death filling the roads. It was truly a great calamity. Zeng Guofan's "Record of the Xiang Army Memorial Shrine in Nanjing" states, "Our army was stationed near Yuhuatai. Before long, epidemics broke out. Brothers fell ill, and younger brothers were infected. They laughed in the morning and stiffened in the evening. After one man died, several accompanied him to the burial. By the time they returned, half had perished on the way." Now, in Shanghai, epidemics have occurred very early after the war. This is also a natural consequence. Now, in the midst of summer, the weather is inconsistently cold and hot, and the air is humid. This is most conducive to the breeding of germs. Once they spread rapidly, the disaster will be no less than war. Alas, for our poor people, the great calamity is not yet over. This is a cause for great concern. There are many charitable organizations in Shanghai. Burying corpses, disinfecting, and preventing epidemics are not tasks for strangers. Giving injections of preventive medicine, providing medicine, and sending doctors are also urgently needed. If the people of the country are eagerly seeking to escape the calamity of war but do not pay attention to the arrival of epidemics, how can it not be dangerous? The method of prevention is nothing more than injecting cholera serum. Also, eating garlic often has a preventive effect. Maintain clean food and drink, exercise the body, do not enter restaurants or playgrounds, do not sleep outdoors under the stars and moon, bathe frequently, sweep and clean often, isolate patients, and disinfect objects. All of these are simple, common sense, but they are effective prescriptions for preventing epidemics. (Note: People who contract epidemic diseases should be sent to the hospital for treatment. Saline injections, etc., are very effective. The various "Ten Drops Water" remedies popular in the market cannot cure genuine cholera. Flies are the sole medium for spreading germs. Therefore, food must be covered to prevent flies from gathering. Also, do not eat spoiled food from the previous day.)

A Strange Woman Who Has Not Eaten for Thirteen Years 104

— Huang Yingdai

It is said that there is a woman in Madurai, India, who is the wife of an Indian weaver. She is thirty years old this year. She has not eaten a drop of water or a bowl of rice for thirteen years. Therefore, people in society pay very close attention to her. Although she has not eaten for thirteen years, her body appears to be very healthy. She has also raised three children. Her story can indeed be compiled into an interesting book. The local officials have recently visited her. It is said that once she was returning to her parents' home from her husband's house, but she suddenly collapsed and fainted on the way. She was later sent to the hospital. She stayed in the hospital for two weeks before returning home. At that time, the doctors used all sorts of methods to make her open her mouth, to make her speak, and to make her eat, but all were ineffective. Her body remained healthy. The doctors had no way of knowing why she fainted and would not speak, so they had to send her back. But after two years, one day she suddenly started talking. Now she helps her husband with household chores at home, but she still does not eat.

Following the marriage of Jiang Menglin and Ms. Tao Zenggu, all eyes were upon them, and it was much discussed; commentators also had mixed opinions. According to reports, Tao was originally the wife of Gao Renshan and was a remarriage; Jiang had been divorced. The wedding ceremony was very simple. Jiang's report highlighted the point that he had "struggled out a path of life from the obligations of love." Hu delivered a speech expressing great admiration for their courage, saying that it "could represent a symbol of an era of change." This tone is quite thought-provoking. Summary of Mid-Year Situation 107

The impact of the war: much less than in previous years. Yesterday was the end of June, which is also the middle of the year. The situation seems much bleaker than last year. February and March of this year were entirely during the wartime period. The commercial strikes to resist aggression and the sluggishness of business were expected. From April to June, there was a gradual recovery, but only for a portion of foreign merchants, which seemed to have improved. On the Chinese merchant side, although there was much more activity on the surface than during the strike, the desolation after the calamity made recovery difficult. Silver and money industries were extremely strict with lending, unable to flow as desired. Therefore, the results of this mid-year closing are far from the prosperity of last year. However, foreign banks are also affected by the economic panic in major foreign ports and cannot be considered a completely prosperous era. However, with collections and settlements of 12 to 13 million, and various foreign exchange items of 6 to 7 million, and cargo pledges of 10 to 20 million, they are still much more prosperous than Chinese merchants. Among them, the entry and exit of Japanese merchant banks account for about 30%. As for the Chinese merchant side, bank collections, excluding settlements of 4 to 5 million and exchange pledges of over 1 million, are only about 30-40% more than usual. The silver dollars from money houses are only 10-20% more. This year, money houses are not making large-scale transactions, which is well known throughout the city, so it is appropriate that the amount is limited.

Recent Tea Market Reports from Anhui and Jiangxi 118

Wuyuan Zi Tea Sales Active, Prices Rise Due to recent demand from various firms and favorable weather, mountain farmers are eager to avoid losing profits on the trees and are hurriedly picking and processing tea. The tea itself has a beautiful color and taste, so firms that were previously indifferent to Zi tea are now paying attention to it. On the 22nd and 23rd of last month, market prices increased by seven to eight yuan compared to the previous two days. Retail prices for mountain farmers range from three to five cents per pound. Farmers, encouraged by the rising tea prices, are hiring workers to help with picking in hopes of increasing production. Tea merchants are also actively searching for and purchasing tea day and night, driven by the potential for profit.

Tunxi Tea Purchases Becoming Scarce Due to the difficulty in raising market prices in recent weeks, the supply of tea from distant areas to Tunxi has been weak. High-grade tea from established firms has seen some recent demand, but prices remain low. Low-grade tea from Anhui, even with prices falling to 22-23 yuan, is rarely sought after. Furthermore, the lack of price increases in the Shanghai market for Zhen tea, with Tunxi tea selling for only 90 taels, has further shrunk the demand for stored tea. In addition, firms have substantial tea reserves from previous purchases, with some holding over 1,000 dan, others 600-700 dan, and the least holding 200-300 dan, sufficient for current production. They are unwilling to increase purchases unless the Shanghai market improves.

Fuliang Zi Tea Sales Brisk Due to the abundant spring tea production this year, tea firms had initially decided to halt Zi tea purchases based on discussions in Shanghai. However, mountain farmers, finding no market with foreign firms, turned to local shops as an alternative outlet. Farmers from various southern villages in Japan are diligently picking, processing, and transporting tea to shops in Jingdezhen, where it sells for three catties per yuan. Shop owners, attracted by the good quality and low prices, are eager to purchase, resulting in a situation where demand exceeds supply.

Oil Market: Tung Oil Trade with Foreign Firms Slightly Active 120

Internal Sales Hampered by Plum Rains Tung oil sales to foreign firms have been slightly active recently. Hankou firms wholesale for domestic sales at around 14 taels and 4 to 6 mace. However, domestic sales have not been strong due to the ongoing plum rains. Hankou's inventory is not particularly large, and with continued foreign sales, the situation is increasingly stable. Therefore, despite weak domestic sales, there is no possibility of lower prices. If domestic sales become active after the plum rains, a bright outlook can be expected. Local firms are continuing to purchase oil, but only to meet immediate demand due to normal sales volumes. They do not seem to be paying attention to timing, and their inventories are not large.

Northeast Post Offices Operating as Usual 122

Authorities Decide to Close Northeast Postal Services

Yesterday, the reporter visited Huang Naishu, Director-General of Posts, to inquire about the details. According to Huang, the latest report received by the Director-General this morning (i.e., yesterday morning) indicated that all post offices in the Northeast were still operating as usual until last night (i.e., the night before) and that there were no changes.
